  1487. # [18:15] <bz> Note that this means that the handlers for a given promise need not be contiguous in this global list

  1491. # [18:15] <bz> So walkerLoop does:
  1492. # [18:15] <bz> 741 while (this.handlers.length > 0) {
  1493. # [18:15] <bz> 742 this.handlers.shift().process();

  1497. # [18:15] * Quits: twi (Adium@moz-11A9D041.cust.vodafonedsl.it) (Connection reset by peer)
  1498. # [18:15] <bz> Before returning to the event loop.
  1499. # [18:16] <bz> DOM promises, on the other hand, have an event loop runnable per promise.
  1500. # [18:16] <bz> And when that runnable fires, all the handlers on that one promise at that point are execute.
  1501. # [18:16] <bz> er, executed.
  1502. # [18:16] <bz> And then we return to the event loop.
  1503. # [18:16] <bz> So the handler invocation order can be quite different.
  1504. # [18:16] <bz> Furthermore, the DOM promise behavior is not actually what the draft spec says to do.
  1505. # [18:16] <bz> which would involve running handlers at microtask checkpoint time, not off the event loop.
  1506. # [18:17] * bz is not sure whether it would run them on a per-promise basis or interleaved more like Promise.jsm; hasn't looked at the spec that closely.
  1507. # [18:17] <bz> So most simply:
